Free Talk

Reading a Few Books 288

— Deng Dangshi

It has long been argued that reading books to death turns one into a bookworm, or even a walking library. As time marches on, the trend against reading has become even more thorough, with some people opposing reading any kind of book. Their basis is Schopenhauer's old saying that reading other people's works is like letting the author ride a horse in your own brain.

This is certainly a wake-up call for those who read books to death, but for geniuses who would rather explore, dance, or be simply agitated, it is a golden saying worth introducing. However, it must be understood that the brain of the genius who clings to this saying is being ridden by Schopenhauer's horse, trampled into a mess.

Now, critics are complaining because there are no better works; creators are also complaining because there is no correct criticism. Zhang San says that Li Si's work is symbolism, so Li Si also believes that it is symbolism, and the reader naturally also believes that it is symbolism. However, what is symbolism? It has never been clarified, so we can only use Li Si's works as evidence. Therefore, what is called symbolism in China is different from what is called Symbolism in other countries, although the former is actually the translation of the latter. However, having heard that Maeterlinck is a symbolic writer, Li Si becomes the Chinese Maeterlinck. In addition, there are many Chinese France, Chinese Babbitt, Chinese Gaultier, Chinese Gorky... However, the translated works of the real France are very few in China. Is it perhaps because there are already "domestic products"?

In the Chinese literary world, the lives of several domestic writers are too long; and the foreign writers are too short. Their names have just become familiar, it is said that they have already passed. Ibsen is expected to have a complete collection, but the third volume is still unseen; Chekhov and Maupassant's selected works also seem to have ended in failure. But in Japan, which we deeply hate, "Don Quixote" and "One Thousand and One Nights" have complete translations: Shakespeare, Goethe, etc. have complete collections: Tolstoy has three kinds, Dostoevsky has two kinds.

Reading books to death is harmful to oneself and harms others as soon as one opens one's mouth; but not reading books is not necessarily good either. At least, for example, if you want to criticize Tolstoy, you must read a few of his works. Of course, now is a time of national crisis, and there is no time to translate these books or read these books, but what I am proposing is to those great men who are only agitated and complaining, not to those heroes who are going to disaster or "sleeping on firewood and tasting gall." Because some people, even if they don't read books, only play and don't go to disaster.

"Spring Floating Garden Diary" 289

— Shu

The "Spring Floating Garden Diary", which describes scenery and the life of a pastoral poet, has some excellent passages. The writing is concise and orderly, seemingly striving to emulate Fang Weng. Several examples are worth mentioning:

(1)

"Ninth day, clear. Transplanted several green plum trees in front of the study, where one can lie and smell them." (2)

"Nineteenth day, clear. Magnolias bloom for the first time, admiring them under the moon, their purity and coldness are indescribable."

(3)

"Fifteenth day. Watched the moon in the lake with guests. After several rounds of wine, there was a slight rain, which gradually became heavier. We ascended the lake pavilion to avoid it. Soon, the wind rose and the water surged. The guests were intolerably cold and all huddled together under blankets. The faint moon, heavy mist, and water trees were shrouded in darkness, creating a strangely beautiful scene. The guests stayed overnight at the Jue Tan Forest, and I stayed at the Bamboo Pavilion, unable to return home." (Xinwei, Spring Floating Garden Occasional Records).

(4)

"Fourth day. Western crabapples are in full bloom, and peaches and plums are also budding. A few daffodils are in bloom, charming and pitiful. In the evening, I visited the Prajna Temple to explore chrysanthemums. The 'Against Frost Yellow' variety is the best, comparable to Ji Gong's 'Golden Finch Tongue'." (Xiao Zhai Diary)

Shi Wei advocated in his writing that "the most difficult thing for a writer is to achieve the realm of plainness. Su Gong said: 'Gradually getting old and experienced, one can create plainness, and only then can one glimpse this.'" (Daily Records). He also said: "Recently, my writing has been simple but lawful." (Spring Floating Garden Occasional Records). These are reflected in his diary, forming a style of plainness and conciseness, with natural and genuine characteristics, worthy of "literary appreciation." The part about social life is very, very little in Shi Wei's diary; like:

"Fourth day. Many people reported early drought. The people's livelihood is deteriorating. Even with a good year, it is still difficult to survive, let alone compounded by war? However, people coming from the north say that after the war, corpses are piled up like mountains, and fires are extinguished. Although there is no year, it is still a happy country." (Occasional Records)

This kind of record is already quite rare. In addition to daily mountain living, flower cultivation, and travel, it also involves books and articles, such as:

"Twelfth day. 'Lying Tour Records' are so rough, I think they were also recorded as ideas arrived, not a complete book. Zhou Gongjin's 'Cheng Huai Records' are also stingy and lack depth. In the evening, after bathing, jasmine flowers bloomed." (Occasional Records).

In addition, there are two or three items on satirical material. On the whole, although Shi Wei's diary strives to emulate Fang Weng, it cannot be compared to the "Entry into Shu Records" in terms of its rich and radiant language and the broadness of the author's scholarship. Moreover, the "Entry into Shu Records" has a value far exceeding that of the "Spring Floating Garden Diary" in cultural history.

At first, I read the "Complete Works of Spring Floating Garden" with the same hope as for the "Jia Xing" and "Flower Viewing" records, wanting to grasp the psychological life of this Ming dynasty remnant. However, I was disappointed. In the diary, except for a preface to "Daily Records of Shen Mu'an", there is nothing; in the collection of poems, there are only a few sentences in "Ascending the Pavilion on the Ninth Day": "Sorrowfully weeping for the old people, the festivals are tired of pure wine;" and the article "Stele Inscription of Longping Mountain Temple". The inscription says:

"The four directions are disturbed by clouds, and there is no complete nest for the clouds: the family and country are lost, and the old country folks are worried. Although the flowing spring is unharmed, and my yang is as before, there is sorrow in the wind and millet, and grief on the road. Even if I want to be like Mr. Zi Gao and embrace this beautiful and refined intention, and write about the desolation of the mountains and rivers, how can it be possible?"

Only these few sentences profoundly express his own depression. In addition to his small essays and diaries, according to the "Preface to Current Essays", there is also a kind of "Drunken Fool's Small Essays", which is a pity that I have not seen. The diary, in the complete collection, includes a total of

(1) "Spring Floating Garden Occasional Records" (Xinwei and Gengwu)

(2) "Bian Tour Records" (Xinwei)

(3) "Xiao Zhai Diary" (namely "Yue Sheng Pavilion Diary"),

(4) "South Return Daily Records" (Dingmao)

(5) "Daily Records of Shen Mu'an" (Guiyou)

A total of five kinds and six volumes, collection of "Xiao Shi Run Yu Xuan". (End)

One Day Diary of Zhuzhou 290

— Tang Xiru

March 6, rainy day. When I got up, the misty rain had covered the fields and barren mountains outside the window with a white haze, leaving only some blurred black outlines. The stationmaster, telegrapher, and office staff had all gone back to their rooms to sleep. Even the switchmen had gone to town: leaving the flag waving lonely in the rain. The trains coming and going here are all at night. As soon as the rooster crows, these many trains, like ghosts, all disappear without a trace. The station is like the hall of a desolate temple, with the scattered footprints of the previous night still on the ground. There is not a single person, should be there are no people nearby? Especially on this kind of rainy day, how desolate! Ah! How desolate it is!

Because it was too lonely to stay at the station alone, I found a travel guide for the Hunan-Hubei Railway to see if there were any famous historical sites nearby. The book said there were the tomb of Lao Laizi and Zifu Temple. Zifu Temple was built by imperial decree in the Tang Dynasty and has been burned and rebuilt many times, so it shouldn't be very interesting. But Lao Laizi's tomb is seventeen or eight miles away from the station. In this desolate mountain village, in this rainy weather, on this muddy road, without knowing the way, without a guide... even if you ask the villagers along the way, they may not all know the sleeping place of the "old child"? Then, should I visit the nearby Zifu Temple? This is how it was decided.

Without an umbrella, I walked two or three miles in the drizzle with my bald head, and Zifu Temple arrived. If it weren't for the three words "Zifu Temple" clearly written on the gatehouse, I would have passed by without knowing it. It is such a small and freshly painted white temple!

This temple is a two-entrance house, with three rooms in each, separated by a patio. Because the back entrance was the auspicious day for the consecration of some Bodhisattva, incense and people filled the room, so I didn't go in, just walked around in the outer entrance. The western room in the outer entrance is a place for storing sundries, full of water trucks and the like, like the works of some cubist painter, it only makes people feel depressed; in the middle is a female Bodhisattva, with a plaque "In the Purple Bamboo Forest", probably Guanyin Bodhisattva; the room on the left is a branch of the town's police station, with a portrait of the Premier hanging in the hall, and a red piece of paper with "Take Office Auspicious" written on it below. In front of the Premier's portrait are incense burners and candle holders. This newly appointed chief should be a fat, squint-eyed, and often laughing funny character? Otherwise, he is just a complete fool.

Just like that, poking my head around, searching everywhere like I had lost my wallet, I finally found some things that could be considered more ancient. It was a stele from the Jiaqing era, with five poems inscribed on it. The first four poems were inscribed by famous people from the Tang and Song dynasties who visited the temple. The fifth poem was the great work of the county magistrate who donated the stele. Chinese literati are the most opportunistic people in the world, and they all care very much about being remembered for generations. This county magistrate, if he lived in present-day China, would probably have published many collections long ago, and would be a powerful figure in the literary world, right?

I took out my notebook and stood in front of the stele to copy the first four poems (with childish mischief, deliberately throwing away the fifth poem). While I was looking and copying, many villagers surrounded me. One villager said loudly behind me:

"The money donated by XXX is all from widows. That widow had an affair with him, and she is using this stinky money to do good deeds. She can't hide it from the Bodhisattva!..."

At first, I was quite strange about the abruptness of these words. Later, I saw a stele in front of me with the names of pious men and women inscribed on it. This remark was probably referring to this. Hastily, I hastily copied the four poems, nodded and smiled at the people surrounding me, and mysteriously broke through the encirclement.

"Chinese people all love 'fame'! The rich, the poor, the educated, the illiterate, everyone wants 'fame', wants permanent 'fame', but they all want to get this permanent good reputation without spending any effort! Chinese people really like to do this kind of business the most!..." Walking and thinking like this, slipping step by step, I returned to the station in a short while.

Brushing off my wet coat, I saw that it was almost twelve o'clock, but the stationmasters had not gotten up yet, so I copied the diary that I hadn't organized for several days.

This small station is really too desolate! It reminds me of a short story by Gorky, "For the Sake of Too Much Monotony." When I came here last night, it was already late at night, and I was sleepy, so I didn't talk to the stationmaster, and I didn't even see his face. Could he be like the protagonist in Gorky's short story?

Just as I was thinking this, the stationmaster came out from behind. It was really "speak of Cao Cao and Cao Cao arrives"! I wanted to laugh out loud, but I managed to hold it back. He said a few words of apology, and then invited me in for a meal.

Because it was the first meal in the morning, and because the stationmaster was also from Jiangsu and Zhejiang, he also prepared porridge. After wandering outside for three or four years, porridge had been temporarily forgotten by me like my hometown. This time, seeing the thick white porridge, I suddenly remembered all the loveliness of my hometown. Although the weather was not cold, I held the bowl and didn't start eating. This breakfast was really the most comfortable meal I had.

Seeing the dishes on the table, they were all very exquisite and rich, so I asked uneasily where all these things came from. He said that he had these many dishes all year round, and that he was a gourmand because the chicken, fish, and meat here were cheaper than elsewhere; there was no place for entertainment here, and he didn't have any habits such as cards and wine, and because of his job, he couldn't easily leave for a day. He was always stationed at this small station, so he vented his loneliness and boredom on the dishes he ate.

After listening to his eating experience, I thought of the protagonist in Gorky's short story again. Their loneliness is the same.

The rain outside the window is always hanging like an annoying fog. Ah, really, this spring rain, I don't know when it will stop.

Shell Gatherers by the Sea 291

— Sha Ming

X X X X X

Is it a dream?

When a misty gust of wind blew on my chest, when the golden sea water reflected in my eyes; the dreamlike illusion vanished unexpectedly. Looking into the distance at the group of shell gatherers,

Golden shells, peach-colored shells:

They are the remnants left behind by life!

X X X X X

The waves are surging and crashing against the steep rocks!

Is it the last struggle of the power of life?

Golden shells, peach-colored shells,

When they flaunt in front of me;

The hope stirred up by emotions,

Suddenly plunged into the longing of misery.

Eugenie (3) 292

— Bai Wei

"What method?" Xuan asked.

"Dear, because you refuse to move elsewhere, I have to move," Eugenie said resolutely and gently.

"Then why bother!" Xuan did not expect the girl to be so determined and immediately gave in. "I'll move then. If you move, not to mention anything else, this piano is heavy enough. If you unfortunately move in with some bad teenagers, I'll be even more worried."

"You're right. I knew you loved me, and you would definitely believe me," Eugenie smiled contentedly.

"When do you want me to move?"

Sure enough, Xuan gave up his room and moved to the Villa Yaju in the 14th arrondissement. The people in the apartment thought that Eugenie and he had broken up! After that, they lived as Eugenie had stipulated. Every Saturday night, Eugenie and Xuan enjoyed themselves thoroughly. Eugenie was very diligent and passed all the oral and written exams in June. She and Xuan toured Paris and the suburbs of Paris for two weeks and went home for the summer vacation.

During the summer vacation, Eugenie's father came to Paris to attend an international academic conference. Because of Eugenie's introduction, he came to visit Xuan. He was a typical father who always wore a morning suit, and Xuan liked him very much. He invited him to taste Chinese food several times and couldn't help but reveal his admiration for Eugenie. Eugenie's father nodded and smiled, knowing the young man's meaning.

When the second school year began, Eugenie returned to Paris. Xuan had already rented half a floor in the suburbs, with two rooms facing a small garden. He welcomed Eugenie to live there. Although he still kept his room in Villa Yaju, he only went there occasionally when he had appointments with other male and female friends. In fact, he was always in the suburbs, accompanying Eugenie. After a long separation, their love became even stronger. Eugenie's ability to read French had increased, and she didn't go to class in the city much, but concentrated on preparing for the exam. They called themselves an engaged couple, and the landlady's family was very envious. The old woman showed her joy for the young couple with extremely attentive hospitality. After the anniversary of Xuan and Eugenie's engagement passed, they both wrote to their families at the same time, officially announcing this love and praying for the approval of both families.

This did not cause much surprise in Eugenie's family, because after her father returned home, Xuan had become the subject of family conversation several times. When Eugenie's letter arrived home, her father and mother's opinions immediately diverged. Her father liked this oriental youth very much; her mother was very opposed. In that rather conservative country, Eugenie's own decision on her husband was considered an encroachment on maternal authority; and Eugenie's choice fell on a foreign youth whom her mother had never met. The fact that it took at least a month to sail from Europe to Shanghai further strengthened her mother's determination to oppose it to the end. Then, the matter was passed from neighbors to the ears of the pastor. The pastor gave Eugenie's parents a special warning: the daughters of the Greek Orthodox Church cannot marry non-believers. Thus, even Eugenie's father did not dare to maintain his support. They had decided to immediately call Eugenie back home, but because of Eugenie's gentle explanation, they still allowed her to stay in Paris to study.

As for Xuan's family, things were even more unfavorable. Xuan's father had always disliked Xuan, especially his marriage problems, which had caused the old man much unhappiness. Xuan had been engaged to a young girl from the Yang family. When Xuan was twenty years old, he corresponded directly with Miss Yang without going through the family and agreed to dissolve the engagement. When the two families ratified the dissolution of the engagement, they also had to settle the economic relations arising from the family relationship. Thus, Xuan's marriage problem had always been a source of annoyance for his father! When he went abroad, his mother warned him against getting close to Western girls. Therefore, the day after his letter stating his love for Eugenie arrived home, his father sent a telegram forbidding him from associating with Eugenie, let alone getting engaged. His mother wrote a letter of calm persuasion, arguing from both emotional and factual standpoints; and said that the family could help him marry a cousin who he had once proposed to but been rejected.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

From Japanese Science Education to Chinese Children's Science 293

— Wan Lücong

The day before yesterday, I saw the section on Mr. Zhou Houxu's impression of Japanese education in the education news column of this newspaper, and I couldn't help but feel deeply ashamed of ourselves for only shouting slogans such as "Down with Japanese imperialism" and "Take back lost territories" without actually doing anything. Can Japanese imperialism be overthrown by mouth? Even if all 450 million Chinese people shouted together, Japanese imperialism would never fall down because of our shouting. They would only laugh at us and get cold teeth.

Mr. Zhou said that we Chinese only talk but don't act, while the Japanese act but don't talk. Of course, the "talk" refers to empty talk. This is an unexaggerated fact. When a Chinese person is slapped in the face, he can't help but open his teeth and scold: the more painful the scolding, the better. It seems that this is already revenge. But they don't know that the one being scolded has already silently prepared to slap the second time, or even prepared to really "do you to death."

This is a fatal wound of the Chinese nation, and it is also a fundamental reason why China is weak and Japan is strong!

Japan has only had a history of fifty or sixty years since the Meiji Restoration, but it has been able to jump from an unnoticed island country to the most noticed and strongest country in the world. It cannot be said that it is not due to their hardworking spirit, doing what they say, and being able to catch up with other people's strengths in practice. It has been twenty or thirty years since the Chinese Revolution, and the reason why it is getting worse and worse is definitely not the weakness of the Chinese people's ability, but the "only talking but not doing."

For example, science. Everyone says that it is the only weapon of national defense in modern countries, and it is an indispensable tool for human life in the future. To relieve national disasters and save China, we can only promote science and popularize science, and the voice of science can be said to be very loud. But in reality, the Chinese scientific community is desolate and makes people shudder. In particular, children's science is even more out of the question. But in Japan, "from elementary school to university, they all pay consistent attention to physics and chemistry." Their teachers guide students to study science with patience and perseverance. Their students are "using their hands and eyes to observe, experiment, collect, and solve problems themselves." They use the laboratory as a classroom, teaching, learning, and doing at the same time. Therefore, it is not without reason that Japan can carry out its barbarous behavior. Moreover, if you go to their bookstores, you will see no less than a dozen scientific magazines specifically for children, not to mention ordinary ones. Although my country has published one or two relatively remarkable scientific magazines in recent years, there is still no trace of any specifically for children.

Japanese imperialism cannot be overthrown by mouth, and national disasters cannot be relieved by mouth. If we really want to overthrow Japanese imperialism and truly save the country from danger, we still have to work hard in practice. History tells us that being rash and shouting slogans is of no avail. Although Japanese imperialism is our eternal enemy, their admirable hardworking spirit of doing what they say is still worthy of our imitation!

On the Cause of Ms. Gong Yinxia's Death (Part 1) 294

— Wei Ci

Ms. Gong Yinxia committed suicide with her children. The reverberation this news must cause in anyone's mind is surely, "excessively tragic!" But how did this excessively tragic event occur? For a person to put themselves in a position of death, and to put the beloved children left behind by her deceased lover to death, creating this rare tragedy, shows that the pain and oppression she suffered in 'life' must have been extremely deep and heavy.

But how did this deep pain and heavy oppression come about? As Mr. Yuan, the author of the Shen Bao commentary on the ninth, said, "It was neither emotional impulse nor economic hardship, but the oppression of the living environment." On the one hand, Ms. Gong was attached to the nest that she had created and managed together with her deceased lover, considering it a place of spiritual sustenance; on the other hand, she was unwilling to be constrained and tormented by the life of a large family. The former, Ms. Gong herself stated explicitly (see her suicide note, which is a possible inner need for a knowledgeable person with a rich emotional life), the latter, we can understand clearly just by looking at Mr. Qin Pingfu's letter, with phrases like "Aunt is merely suspicious and trivial... all the sisters are married off... tactful accommodation... being strict with oneself and lenient with others... magnanimous..." It tells us that the inevitable contradictions and conflicts in every large family were no exception in that family. Ms. Gong felt the pain of not wanting to leave her home in Shanghai and not wanting to be merged into the home in Wuxi, so on April 11th, after receiving a letter from her father-in-law, after April 15th (seven weeks after February 25th), she even went to Mr. Yuan to discuss her children's schooling and her own career issues. This should be an attempt to dissuade the proposal to return to Wuxi, in order to eliminate the pain she would suffer, which is also a side proof of the more than ten times she wanted to commit suicide but stopped. But in the end, she was oppressed by irresistible pressure, which made her unable to bear the accusations of "division", "harming feelings", "adding to the burden", not being "magnanimous", etc. She was saddened by the destruction of her independent life, and even her independent personality was doubted, so in the end, she had no choice but to escape all suffering by suicide.

Based on the above reasoning, it can be said that Ms. Gong's death was also after a struggle, and she inevitably died because she could not have both!

However, this is entirely an analysis of her behavior from Ms. Gong's own thoughts. If we judge her by the "rational standard of living," then her behavior is completely wrong. Although she yearned for a rational life, her thinking was not enough to guide her on how to protect her demands: for example, a woman with bound feet is not fundamentally unable to wade through water and climb mountains, but the long strips of cloth destroy her ability. If Ms. Gong had natural feet, if she had not been bound by feudal ideas and had been fully nurtured in the new world and accepted new ideas, then the oppression she suffered would not have become oppression at all. We analyze the reasons why the Qin family insisted on Ms. Gong returning to Wuxi: on the one hand, they wanted to combine the property to generate profits and accumulate wealth (silently reverse the fortune; therefore, they must "return to Wuxi to save expenses, and save a penny today to reduce the burden on the eldest grandson in the future"); on the other hand, they may have thought that a middle-aged widow living in a prosperous city was not proper. Therefore, he, as the head of the family, with the authority to manage the property of the widow and interfere with the actions of the widow, insisted that his daughter-in-law return home, and even found a reason of "the deceased's soul has a command" to be the rear guard. These great principles that were considered sacred and inviolable in feudal society must be known to have been denied and overthrown today. If Ms. Gong was a person who had accepted new ideas and had a clear understanding of the current society, recognizing that people in the current society, especially women in the current society, should only follow reason in everything, not compromise, and not live in ease. If it is contrary to the truth, then fight with the spirit of revolution. Then, she would not consider destroying the economic system of the large family as a fault, or helping the economic development of the large family as her duty, or accumulating more inheritance for her descendants as a blessing for her descendants, or disobeying the orders of her in-laws as a damage to virtue; nor would she believe that her deceased husband could still issue orders in the "underworld". What she should consider her only duty is to maintain personal independence, seek the development of personal ability, and do her best to ensure that her children receive a good education, so that they become useful talents for society. If she had this understanding, and acted according to her inner demands, then would she still need to be distressed and hesitant, unable to cope, and eventually commit suicide? (To be continued)

Impressions of the City God Temple 295

— Wen Xin

Upon entering the City God Temple, one vaguely feels that in Shanghai, which is full of Western influence, the City God Temple is a place where one can better savor the unique style of China. Although everything is in a slump now, the City God Temple is still as lively as ever, and there is no sign of decline. Every day, it is crowded with people, continuously entering and exiting to visit and admire. When you first enter, you may feel that there is nothing spectacular, but if you look carefully, there are some things that are not entirely ordinary. It seems that within the plain and vulgar scenery, there is an infinite hidden charm. Some of the elegant styles of antiques make people feel the civilized ancient country and think of today's sick man of Asia, and have endless feelings of melancholy!

After leaving the City God Temple, the impressions that remain in my mind, apart from this bit of desolate feeling, are the gods and women there that I find interesting. The countless Buddhas there are indeed the main scenery! The air of incense is even thicker. Passing by, my eyes almost teared up from the smoke. Speaking of liveliness, this is the most prominent place. The women who worship gods are so numerous that it makes people laugh. Each of them puts on a very serious look, solemnly holding the burning incense in their hands, right in front of their chest. They also have a bag hanging on their bodies, like the ones monks and nuns use for begging for alms, presumably meaning that you must hang it on your body to worship the gods. From the left side to the right side, from the front to the back, passing by each other, all are the same kind of women. Silently muttering in their mouths; after inserting the incense and kneeling down to kowtow, they put their hands together and bow to each of the Buddhas, big and small. Sometimes when you pass by the Buddhas, you are lucky enough to enjoy a few bows as well. They worship all kinds of different

Page 20

Page 21

Page 22

Page 23

Buddhas, all reciting words, asking for wishes. It seems to have become a very tasteless daily routine, giving a somewhat inexplicable feeling. After feeling amused for a while, I think about why it is completely women who worship gods, and there are almost no men. On the one hand, I feel that the fate of the gods is still prosperous, with so many people sincerely taking the trouble to worship them, still representing the strong existence of feudal meaning; but on the other hand, I also seem to feel that only women worship gods so enthusiastically, while men do not worship gods, then it can show that gods are gradually declining, superstition is gradually being eliminated, and men are more active in society, so they are mostly swept away by the realities of life and worship gods less, with only women remaining immersed in dreams in the ghost stories of gods, which is somewhat gratifying. However, the problem is not so simple, how will the fate of the gods decline now! I heard that in my hometown, adults are chanting about returning to the past. From returning to the past to worshiping gods and Buddhas, it seems that in the absence of other options, returning to the past and welcoming gods can temporarily become a countermeasure, serving as a way to save the times. I cannot help but think again about the prosperity of the gods in the City God Temple, which is a relatively unique style of sentiment in today's world.

A Fu 296

— Qing

A Fu's wife has been dead for a whole month. During this month, his life has been extremely difficult and painful. Not only does he have to cook and wash his own clothes after getting off work, but he also has to decoct medicine and wash diapers for his four-year-old child, who has been sick for two weeks. Although he has only lived this kind of life for a short month, he is indeed tired enough. In the middle of the night, when he is awakened from his drowsy sleep by his child's crying, he always sighs sadly, calling out to his wife, and complaining about his hard life.

In the past two days, his child's illness has become even more severe. He cries and screams all day long, and his small body is almost burning dry. His thin, dark face is covered with a layer of ochre, and his eyes seem to have lost their luster. A Fu has taken leave from work to take care of his poor child at home. He exchanged a pair of gold-plated rings left behind by his wife for one yuan and two jiao, and took his child to see the doctor several times, but the child is still sick. He is so anxious that he has no ideas. He invited Li Mama, who lives next door, to come over and asked her what he should do. Li Mama said that if the fever does not go down all day like this, it must not be effective to take medicine. It is probably because the time is bad and he has encountered some ghosts and gods. So she told him not to take his child to see the doctor anymore, because it would be a waste of time. He should go to Qingliang Temple to ask the gods, ask for a fairy prescription to try, and buy more tin foil money and paper at night. Ask Granny Wang to restrain the gods and drive away the ghosts. Then, he will definitely get better tomorrow. A Fu accepted Li Mama's advice with tears in his eyes and a heart full of suffering. He entrusted his crying child lying on the bed to Li Mama, and took a quilt from the bed that was covered with many urine stains and had holes revealing the dark wadding, and went out.

Three hours later, A Fu ran home panting with sweat all over his head. The tattered and dark quilt had been exchanged for four mao of small coins. Together with the four mao he had in his pocket, he made eight mao, bought a few pieces of tin foil, a bundle of paper money, and also brought four pieces of soy sauce meat and a packet of peanuts, which were prepared for Granny Wang to drink while performing a ritual to drive away ghosts for his child tonight. He also took out the fairy prescription from his arms. The so-called fairy prescription was a piece of yellow paper, on which it was written crookedly to decoct water with yellow soil from the stove and licorice to give to the child. On the day after taking the fairy prescription and Granny Wang performing a ritual to drive away ghosts, their child was indeed much quieter. Not only did he not cry and scream, but he also did not ask for food or drink. He was just drowsy and immersed in sleep. It took a lot of effort and methods to wake him up. Touching his small forehead, it was still hot and burning on the palm of his hand. Therefore, A Fu felt that this situation was too quiet, and felt an unnamed anxiety and fear in his heart. He went to ask his high neighbor Li Mama for advice again with a bag of tears in his eyes. Li Mama came to see him again, still acting old-fashioned, bulging her two dry lips, and said reasonably: "Brother A Fu, it doesn't matter, don't worry. The fairy prescription will only take effect after a day and a night. If the child wants to sleep, let him sleep. Don't yell at him. It's pitiful. Didn't you say that he has been noisy all night until dawn for seven or eight days? He is so young, he should be tired. Let him be quiet. I tell you, doctors are the most unreliable. I have lived this long and have never seen a doctor. Every time my back aches, I just ask for a fairy prescription and eat it, and it will be fine. Fairy prescriptions are really effective." Li Mama said confidently while covering the child with a blanket.

On that very night, from two o'clock, the child lying on the bed changed. At first, he was just humming with his teeth clenched, then slowly clenched his fists, rolled his eyes, rolled around on the bed, and shouted with a straight voice in his throat. A Fu had no other way, just calling out "My good child!" helplessly, and teardrops dripped on his hot little body.

By the time it was almost dawn, the child's throat was stuck with phlegm, gurgling and speeding up his breathing. After another half an hour, the child stopped breathing. A Fu knew it was not going to work, so he cried loudly in grief.

Unknowingly, A Fu had not gone to work in the factory for a week. At this time, in order to have money to take care of his poor child, he remembered that he had not received a week's wages from the factory. He calculated that he would spend these four yuan, and then beg Accountant Zhou for an advance of a week's wages, probably eight yuan, which would be enough for the burial and to hire a Taoist priest to chant some scriptures, because he only had one child, and he was the only one left alone in the future, so he didn't want to be too sloppy with the child.

He staggered into the factory early in the morning. There were only a few people in the factory. The watchman did not allow him to enter and asked him who he was looking for. He said that he was the factory's coppersmith, and his child had died. He wanted to borrow some money from Accountant Zhou. The watchman told him that he had taken too long of a leave, and the factory could not stop working. The foreman had already found a new worker to fill in. He also told him that his nameplate had been removed three hours after he took leave.

A Fu was shocked by this unexpected and great stimulus and almost fainted. He thought, "I work like a horse all year round. My child is sick and died. Shouldn't I take leave? Is it too much to take leave without pay?" This damn society, damn people, damn foreman! I'll kill him when I see him!" A pure, kind and honest A Fu was now like a tyrant, a mad dog, his eyes full of blood, clenching his fists and looking around, as if looking for someone to tear apart.

Near the factory, he waited for a long time. He saw men, women and children carrying baskets and entering the factory happily. Many of them were usually on good terms with him. He ran over to greet them. Some of them just said good morning to him, some ignored him, and some even smiled lightly at him. This threat was extremely great to him, so his dangerous and terrible thoughts became even more profound. He saw a pregnant man in a student uniform coming from afar. He recognized that the person coming was his enemy. He hid in a dark place, let the pregnant man walk past, picked up a stone, caught up and threw it at the back of the man's head. The man was knocked down.

At lunchtime that day, A Fu's neighbors were spreading the rumor that A Fu had beaten someone to death and had been arrested by the Public Security Bureau.

Biography of Bu Ruyi (4) 297

— Forget Self

Thoughts by the Window 298

— Nai

Shanghai has no spring, and my heart has even less spring!

I have been living in this dungeon-like Shanghai for seven years, and he has passed seven springs. However, in Shanghai, I have never seen a spring. The four seasons seem to be the same, without autumn or winter. If there is any, it can only be tasted carefully in the activity of people, especially in the trembling posture of women. However, this is too bitter after all, I am so unlucky with women!

This is beyond my expectations. I live in such a high building, the quiet environment and the open window make me feel unusually comfortable. After work every day, I lean on the window to look into the distance, venting the accumulated depression in my chest and staring at the cluttered external scenery. In this way, although I sometimes seem like a infatuated person, I only have such a comfortable mood. I have no unreasonable thoughts and no expectations.

This is even more beyond my expectations. Recently, I found a lithe and graceful girl in a thatched cottage far outside the window. Her figure is so slender and soft, and her attitude is so gentle and innocent. The first time I saw her, I didn't care, because I was sure that she was not a product of the thatched cottage, but a dancing star from someone's house. However, I see her shadow every day when I look out the window. So, "Gradually, I began to have a heart of affection. Her frequent glances clearly express her thoughts. She is not like ordinary women who hate people like us!"

In order to obtain this little bit of ethereal comfort, I feel that Shanghai actually has a spring this year, as if I see spring dancing in front of the window. In fact, spring has already left the world, and now it is summer. My heart is even more filled with spring, washing away the accumulated depression of the past few years, my heart is jumping every moment, and life seems to have added a bit of vigor. But ah, I only have this little bit of affection, because I have already······

Girl, please cherish the spring in the world! I have no unreasonable thoughts and no expectations!

It is Time 299

— He Juefu

Last year, Tingtao Society published a book called "Words of the Meat-Eaters". Although I have not personally read it, according to friends, what is collected inside are the speeches made by those in power today when they were out of office. What these remarks are saying, I have not seen with my own eyes, so of course I dare not blindly speculate; but, if someone is willing to spend some time carefully reading it, they may also get a strange feeling!

There is no need to mention this, because I am not a hero with copper skin and iron bones who can fly over walls and walk on eaves. Now let's look back at the literary scene of our country in the past ten years:

In the "May Fourth" era, due to the influence of Western European liberal thought and the rise of the domestic bourgeoisie, a group of brave warriors carried out a movement of destruction of form to liberation of content against our country's "literature of morality" that had existed for thousands of years. This movement did achieve considerable success, and this group of brave warriors also rose to prominence as a result.

In the "May 30th" era, due to the agitation of the revolutionary upsurge, the trend of literature underwent another major change. In this change, a new group of heroes was able to ascend the throne.

The achievements of the warriors of the "May Fourth" era and the heroes of the "May 30th" era in overthrowing the old forces and establishing new literature at that time cannot be easily denied by anyone; but, now that they have achieved fame and fortune, what are they doing again?

We are not colorblind, we can see very clearly: among them, some have inexplicably started playing with antiques, writing ancient-style regulated poems, and giving each other gifts to show their elegance; some have surrendered to powerful families, writing servile articles praising their merits to please their masters; some are unrestrained and comfortable, playing in the mountains and rivers, singing about the wind and moon, and casually writing travel notes and miscellaneous feelings to entertain themselves? Not only the heroic spirit of the "May Fourth" and "May 30th" eras has long since disappeared; they also don't care what era it is now, or what impact this will have on the entire literary scene.

Some people say that the phenomenon in our country's literary scene is not much different from the situation in our country's officialdom. I dare not say whether this statement is correct or not. But, if someone were to ask these authoritative writers who have become immortals why they change so much, I believe that their answer would indeed be: "It was one time, and this is another time!"

This is "time", everyone believes; but, will the long flow of time stop from now on? I dare not say, and in fact there is no need for me to say.

Educators, Prepare Yourselves! 300

— Hu Lei

One

"Education is omnipotent!" This is the view of Chinese scholar-officials. They try to use education to lead society and transform society, but the facts tell them that this is an illusion, just an illusion! They did not understand that education is the upper structure of society, and education is evolving there, following politics, especially economics.

Two

In this extremely dangerous environment, there are a group of educators who, when they realize that education is only a tool and cannot lead or transform society, become disappointed and sad, thinking that educators have no way to go.

Have educators really run out of options? No, absolutely not! There are many jobs waiting for educators in the field of education!

Three

Educators, prepare yourselves, prepare to shoulder the great historical mission assigned to you. The power of educators is limited today, but you must fulfill the responsibility that history has given you. Educators should do the preparatory work for social transformation.

At present, there are few considerable organizations for educators who have the same or similar ideas. Even if there are organizations, the motivation comes from people who are obsessed with heroism and messianism, which is very wrong. The organization that true educators should have is as solid as iron, and at the same time, it is an organization of the masses. In the organization, there are no heroes and no disciples!

At present, it is impossible for educators to have an organization with a certain mode in order to form a force. We can only make use of the environment and change the organization mode according to the environment.

Four

Educators, prepare yourselves! Prepare for the work of social transformation! Organize first!

Li Cheng's Marital Entanglement 302

— Editor's Note

Of course, most marital entanglements these days stem from the flaws in the marriage system itself, and the parties involved are all "victims of a society in transition between the old and the new."

However, if we consider whether the "sacrifice" can be remedied, undoubtedly women still suffer more. Not divorcing, as Mr. Li says, causes pain to both parties, but after a divorce, the man can escape the sea of ​​suffering and be freed from "the pain inflicted by this unreasonable union," but what about the woman? Her suffering is even greater than if she hadn't divorced. This can be seen from Ms. Cheng's first letter: "I have three reasons for not wanting a divorce: First, I don't want to... If he divorces me, he can become a new groom, but I can't become a new bride. Second, after reading about the stepmother in 'Konggu Lan' (Empty Valley Orchid) who cruelly beats the son born to Ren Zhu, I worry that if I divorce, my two children will also suffer this pain. Third, my family is not a lower-class family... and I have not done anything bad. My parents would lose face if I divorced." The second and third concerns, though difficult to avoid in reality, do have remedies. As for the "first reason for not wanting," it is indeed a major problem. Mr. Li believes that not divorcing is "making her live as a widow," but if they divorce, can he remarry without suffering "the cruel punishment of living a lonely life"? In this society, it is probably very difficult.

Therefore, in today's society, there is no appropriate and satisfactory remedy for marital entanglements. Mr. Li's views are very correct on this point. But I personally always believe that in an unreasonable marriage like this, the husband should sacrifice a little more. Even if the wife is very old-fashioned and the two parties simply cannot connect, he should not focus entirely on his own interests and rashly talk about divorce, let alone neglect her because he "loves someone new." Family happiness is indeed of great importance in life, but life is not entirely for the sake of love. Those who lack love can seek satisfaction and compensate for this deficiency in other aspects. Adam Smith remained unmarried throughout his life, but his spirit was not necessarily "extremely miserable." He regarded his academic achievements as the source of his happiness, transferring his marital love to academics. Of course, we do not expect everyone to be able to do this, but isn't it obvious that an unhappy marriage does not mean the complete loss of a person's happiness?

In addition, regarding the three questions you asked, they have been frequently discussed in the mailbag section, so I won't go into detail. Don't say that I arbitrarily assumed you "have someone new." I want to declare to you that I am indeed basing this on her "one-sided statement," but judging from the facts stated in her first letter, I'm afraid it is by no means fabricated. Editor

Fiction

The Poor Gentleman (10) 303

— Written by George Gissing of England, translated by Sun Pu

The cheque was crossed. Mr. Dymond, for the first time in his life, realized that a crossed cheque could cause great trouble to the recipient. How was he to change it? His landlord was an eccentric miser, and Mr. Sharg's refusal to help, accompanied by the look he gave, would be a pure humiliation to him; moreover, it was highly doubtful whether Mr. Sharg himself could use the cheque. Who else could he entrust it to? Truly, there was no one in the city of London.

Oh, the first thing to do was to answer Mrs. Woolf's letter. He lit the lamp and sat at the dilapidated small pine table; but his pen, dipped repeatedly into the ink bottle, still could not find words to write.

"Dear Mrs. Woolf," 丨丨

Then, he stopped for a long time, as if he had dozed off for a while. Suddenly perking up, he began to write eagerly again.

"With sincere gratitude, I received your most kind and generous donation. This sum of money..."

(His hand rested again for several minutes.)

"...will be used as you wish, and I will send you a detailed account of the gift bestowed."

He had never felt that writing was so difficult. He felt that he was expressing himself very unsatisfactorily, and his mind was clogged. Finishing this letter required all his physical strength. After finishing the letter, he went out, bought a stamp at the tobacconist's, and then dropped the letter in the mailbox.

Mr. Dymond barely slept that night. As soon as he lay in bed, he began to think about where he would find the poor people worthy of sharing this kindness. Of course, he did not know the class of people Mrs. Woolf thought he knew. In a sense, all the families around were poor, but 丨he asked himself丨did poverty have the same meaning for them as it did for him? In this dirty street, were there any men and women who could rightfully call themselves poor compared to him? A educated man, forced to live among these lower classes, had reached all sorts of interesting conclusions about these lower classes: one conclusion had long been fixed in Mr. Dymond's mind, namely, that the "suffering" of these classes was greatly exaggerated by observers according to an extremely inappropriate standard. Around him, he saw a crude form of amusement, satisfying labor, and a brutal, insensitive world. In his opinion, almost undoubtedly, he was the only one in this street who felt poverty and suffered from poverty.
